**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is May, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Now, Elon Musk is leaving his role as the head of DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

====================Input File Start====================

**All following Reddit news posts are from the subreddit r/politics.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:
Breaking political news
Opinion pieces and editorials
Legislation and policy discussions
Elections, political figures, and government actions

It's moderated to focus on U.S.-centric content and generally avoids memes or low-effort posts. The subreddit can have a progressive or liberal-leaning tone, depending on the community's engagement, though it hosts a range of political perspectives.

**Step 1 (logic-heavy)**

Define the Categories: 

Read through the titles of hundreds of news articles and think carefully.  Use your memory fully. Define major areas, and define specific topics under each area, in a hierarchical way. You should consider this very carefully, making the categories the most helpful for human cognition. Control the total number of areas to 5-8, depending on how diverse and complex the topics are. ### **TOP-LINE SUMMARY**

**Date:** May 24, 2025
**To:** Congressional Leadership (Democratic & Republican)
**From:** Chief News Analyst
**RE:** Daily Intelligence Briefing

Good morning. The nation faces a convergence of high-stakes crises that demand immediate attention. The most acute threat is external, with the President actively debating military action against Iran, a move that is creating deep, public fissures within his political base and stands in stark contrast to U.S. intelligence assessments. Domestically, the administration is escalating its use of military personnel for immigration enforcement, leading to the high-profile arrests of public figures, widespread protests under the "No Kings" banner, and significant legal challenges to the scope of executive authority. ### **Area 1: The Iran Crisis**

**1.1. White House Debating Imminent Military Action**

The administration is at a critical decision point regarding potential military intervention against Iran, an event being framed as a "pivotal moment" for the presidency [1]. High-level White House deliberations reportedly include the possibility of the United States joining Israel in direct strikes against Iranian nuclear facilities [2]. This aggressive option is being actively considered. While weighing this momentous step, President Trump has made public statements tempering expectations of an immediate decapitation strike, remarking to the press, "We won’t kill ayatollah — for now" [3]. Behind the scenes, a "Pro-Israel U.S. General" is reported to be quietly exerting significant influence on the President's calculus, pushing a hawkish line [4]. This combination of public posturing and private debate indicates that the potential for conflict remains exceptionally high and could be triggered with little warning.

**1.2. U.S. Intelligence and Military Dissent**

A significant and concerning gap has emerged between the White House's public posture and the formal assessments of the intelligence community and military leadership. U.S. spy agencies have reportedly concluded that Iran is not actively building a nuclear weapon, an assessment the President is said to publicly dismiss [1]. This fundamental analytical divergence is compounded by operational dissent from within the armed forces. The U.S. Navy reportedly opposed the recent push to reposition strategic assets toward the Middle East, signaling friction within the Pentagon over the rush toward a potential conflict [2]. In a further sign of an internal disconnect, Director of National Intelligence Tulsi Gabbard was reportedly not invited to key Camp David meetings convened to discuss the escalating conflict. According to one report, she was never invited in the first place, a move that suggests she is being sidelined from the core national security decision-making process [3].

**1.3. Deep Fissures Emerge in "MAGA World" and Across Parties**

The prospect of war with Iran is creating profound political divisions that are fracturing the President's own base of support. Reports describe a "bitter split" forming within "MAGA world," as some of the movement's most prominent figures are now openly rebuking the President's direction on Iran [1, 2]. This dangerous schism has been amplified by a sudden and public feud between President Trump and Tucker Carlson, a development that has "deeply rattled" many loyal supporters and threatens to weaken the administration's political flank at a critical moment [3]. While this intra-party conflict intensifies, some voices on the Democratic side are taking a hawkish stance. Senator John Fetterman, for example, stated unequivocally that Israel "100 percent" should have targeted Iran’s supreme leader in its recent actions, highlighting that pressure for escalation is not an exclusively Republican position [4].

**1.4. Iran's Response and U.S. Public Opinion**

Tehran has responded to the administration's threats with defiant public statements. Supreme Leader Ayatollah Khamenei declared that his country "cannot surrender" to American pressure [1]. This posture has been reinforced by official government warnings stating that any direct U.S. military intervention in the ongoing conflict would be a "'recipe for all-out war'" [2]. Meanwhile, the American public shows little appetite for such a conflict. Recent polling indicates that a strikingly low 16% of Americans want the U.S. to become militarily involved in the Israel-Iran war [3]. This sentiment extends deep into the President's own base, with another poll suggesting that over half of Trump voters are opposed to a U.S. war with Iran, revealing a significant disconnect between the administration's deliberations and the will of the electorate [4].

### **Area 2: Domestic Security & Civil Unrest**

**2.1. Escalation of Domestic Military and ICE Operations**

The administration is actively deploying U.S. military troops for domestic law enforcement, signaling a major escalation in its immigration and security strategy. Reports confirm the activation of 2,000 additional military troops to be deployed to the city of Los Angeles [1]. Concurrently, 700 troops have been separately mobilized to provide direct assistance to U.S. Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) for raids in the states of Florida, Louisiana, and Texas [2]. These ground-level operations are creating significant disruption, with American industry leaders now reportedly pleading with the White House for "relief from raids" that are impacting their workforce and operations [3]. The use of active-duty military personnel to support federal law enforcement on U.S. soil marks a significant and highly controversial expansion of executive action.

The administration’s intensified security posture is facing immediate and forceful challenges in the courts and on the streets. Recent ICE operations have resulted in the detention of at least one elected official, NYC Comptroller and mayoral candidate Brad Lander. His arrest sparked "chaos" and public outrage amid questions over whether federal agents possessed a valid judicial warrant for the action [1, 2]. In a separate but related incident, a Spanish-language journalist known for documenting immigration raids was also detained by ICE following an arrest at a protest [3]. These actions are being met with fierce legal resistance; a federal judge has already found the Florida attorney general in contempt of court for defying a judicial order in a major immigration case [4]. In response, the Department of Justice is asserting sweeping executive power, arguing in the 9th Circuit that the President's authority to deploy the National Guard to "quell the rebellion" cannot be "second-guessed by judges" [5]. Early reports suggest the appeals court appears "poised to side with Trump" in this specific case, setting the stage for a constitutional showdown over the limits of presidential power [6].

**From:** Chief News Analyst

Good morning. The nation faces a convergence of high-stakes crises that demand immediate attention. The most acute threat is external, with the President actively debating military action against Iran, a move that is creating deep, public fissures within his political base and stands in stark contrast to U.S. intelligence assessments. Domestically, the administration is escalating its use of military personnel for immigration enforcement, leading to the high-profile arrests of public figures, widespread protests under the "No Kings" banner, and significant legal challenges to the scope of executive authority. ### **Area 1: The Iran Crisis**

**1.1. White House Debating Imminent Military Action**

The administration is at a critical decision point regarding potential military intervention against Iran, an event being framed as a "pivotal moment" for the presidency [1]. High-level White House deliberations reportedly include the possibility of the United States joining Israel in direct strikes against Iranian nuclear facilities [2]. This aggressive option is being actively considered. While weighing this momentous step, President Trump has made public statements tempering expectations of an immediate decapitation strike, remarking to the press, "We won’t kill ayatollah — for now" [3]. Behind the scenes, a "Pro-Israel U.S. General" is reported to be quietly exerting significant influence on the President's calculus, pushing a hawkish line [4]. This combination of public posturing and private debate indicates that the potential for conflict remains exceptionally high and could be triggered with little warning.

## 4. Domestic Economic & Social Issues

### 4.1. Federal Budget Crisis and Agency Staffing Collapse

Severe fiscal pressures and associated staffing shortages are threatening core government functions. A new House policy bill is now projected to add a staggering $3.4 trillion to the national debt, an amount that economic analysis suggests would swamp any corresponding economic gains from the legislation [1]. This fiscal strain is materializing as a staffing crisis in key federal agencies. The Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (CDC) has reportedly "shed one-quarter of its staff," a catastrophic loss of institutional knowledge. The agency has been forced to argue in court that these cuts do not cause "irreparable harm" to states, even as its own leaders lament the resulting "loss of expertise and capacity" [2]. The consequences are tangible and severe, with both domestic and international effects. The potential termination of the federal Job Corps program now risks homelessness for thousands of young Americans [3]. Furthermore, reports indicate U.S. funding cuts have "demolished" South Africa's advanced medical research capabilities, which were previously supported by the U.S. government [4].

An incident of political violence in Minnesota has elevated concerns among U.S. lawmakers about their personal safety.
